## Chapter 1:3: Chinese Approach to International Law:




### Introduction

China's approach to international organizations has been a topic of great interest and debate in the international community. As one of the world's largest and most influential countries, China's role in global organizations has a significant impact on the global political landscape. In this chapter, we will explore the Chinese approach to international organizations, examining their policies, strategies, and impact on the global stage.

China's involvement in international organizations has been a key aspect of its foreign policy since the 1970s. As a rising global power, China has sought to establish itself as a responsible and influential member of the international community. This has been reflected in its approach to international organizations, where China has actively participated and contributed to various global initiatives.

One of the key principles guiding China's approach to international organizations is the concept of non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries. This principle has been a cornerstone of Chinese foreign policy and has been consistently upheld in its interactions with international organizations. China has also emphasized the importance of mutual respect and equality in its relationships with other countries, particularly in the context of international organizations.

In recent years, China's role in international organizations has become increasingly significant. As a permanent member of the United Nations Security Council, China has played a crucial role in shaping global policies and addressing global challenges. China's economic power has also allowed it to play a leading role in organizations such as the World Trade Organization and the International Monetary Fund.

In this chapter, we will delve deeper into China's approach to international organizations, examining its policies, strategies, and impact on the global stage. We will also explore the challenges and opportunities that China's involvement in international organizations presents for the international community. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of China's role in global organizations and its impact on the international political landscape.




### Subsection: 14.1a Role of International Organizations in Foreign Policy

International organizations play a crucial role in shaping China's foreign policy. These organizations provide a platform for China to engage with other countries on a wide range of issues, from trade and security to human rights and environmental protection. China's approach to these organizations is guided by its principles of non-interference and mutual respect, which it sees as essential for maintaining stability and promoting cooperation in the international community.

One of the key international organizations that China is a member of is the United Nations (UN). As a permanent member of the UN Security Council, China has a significant influence on global security issues. It has consistently advocated for a peaceful resolution of conflicts and has opposed the use of force in international relations. China's approach to the UN reflects its broader foreign policy principle of non-interference, which it sees as a way to respect the sovereignty of other countries and avoid exacerbating conflicts.

In addition to the UN, China is also a member of numerous other international organizations, including the World Trade Organization (WTO), the International Monetary Fund (IMF), and the World Health Organization (WHO). These organizations play a crucial role in shaping China's economic and social policies, as they provide a forum for China to engage with other countries on issues such as trade, finance, and health.

China's involvement in these organizations has also allowed it to play a leading role in addressing global challenges. For example, China has been a key player in the WHO's efforts to combat the spread of diseases such as SARS and Ebola. It has also been a major contributor to the IMF's efforts to stabilize global financial markets.

However, China's involvement in international organizations has not been without controversy. Some critics argue that China's policies and actions within these organizations, particularly in areas such as human rights and environmental protection, do not align with its rhetoric of non-interference and mutual respect. They argue that China's economic power and growing influence in these organizations have allowed it to avoid accountability for its actions.

Despite these criticisms, China's approach to international organizations remains a key aspect of its foreign policy. As China continues to rise as a global power, its role in these organizations will only become more significant. Understanding China's approach to international organizations is therefore crucial for understanding its foreign policy and its role in shaping the global political landscape.





### Subsection: 14.1b Chinese Approach to International Organizations

China's approach to international organizations is guided by its principles of non-interference and mutual respect. These principles are rooted in China's long history of valuing sovereignty and non-interference in the internal affairs of other states. China sees these principles as essential for maintaining stability and promoting cooperation in the international community.

One of the key international organizations that China is a member of is the United Nations (UN). As a permanent member of the UN Security Council, China has a significant influence on global security issues. It has consistently advocated for a peaceful resolution of conflicts and has opposed the use of force in international relations. China's approach to the UN reflects its broader foreign policy principle of non-interference, which it sees as a way to respect the sovereignty of other countries and avoid exacerbating conflicts.

In addition to the UN, China is also a member of numerous other international organizations, including the World Trade Organization (WTO), the International Monetary Fund (IMF), and the World Health Organization (WHO). These organizations play a crucial role in shaping China's economic and social policies, as they provide a forum for China to engage with other countries on issues such as trade, finance, and health.

China's involvement in these organizations has also allowed it to play a leading role in addressing global challenges. For example, China has been a key player in the WHO's efforts to combat the spread of diseases such as SARS and Ebola. It has also been a major contributor to the IMF's efforts to stabilize global financial markets.

However, China's involvement in international organizations has not been without controversy. Some critics argue that China's policies and actions within these organizations do not align with its stated principles of non-interference and mutual respect. For instance, China has faced criticism for its human rights record and its treatment of ethnic minorities, such as the Uighurs in Xinjiang. These issues have led to tensions with other member states, particularly the United States, and have raised questions about China's true intentions in these organizations.

Despite these criticisms, China remains a key player in international organizations and continues to shape global policies and initiatives. Its approach to these organizations reflects its broader foreign policy goals of promoting stability, economic development, and its own national interests. As China's global influence continues to grow, its approach to international organizations will likely remain a crucial aspect of its foreign policy strategy.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to international organizations. We have seen how China's foreign policy is shaped by its historical and cultural background, as well as its current economic and political interests. China's approach to international organizations is characterized by a combination of cooperation and competition, with a focus on promoting its own interests while also maintaining stability and avoiding conflict.

China's involvement in international organizations has been steadily increasing over the years, reflecting its growing global influence. From joining the United Nations in 1971 to becoming a founding member of the Shanghai Cooperation Organization in 2001, China has actively participated in various international organizations. This has allowed it to shape global policies and regulations to better suit its own interests.

However, China's approach to international organizations has also faced criticism. Some argue that China's actions in these organizations, such as its support for authoritarian regimes and its lack of transparency, go against the principles of international cooperation and human rights. Others argue that China's growing influence in these organizations could lead to a shift in global power dynamics, potentially causing instability and conflict.

Despite these criticisms, China's approach to international organizations remains a crucial aspect of its foreign policy. As China continues to rise as a global power, its involvement in international organizations will only become more significant. It is essential for China to navigate these organizations carefully, balancing its own interests with the interests of other member states, to maintain stability and promote cooperation in the international community.

## Chapter: Chinese Foreign Policy: International Relations and Strategy

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, international organizations play a crucial role in shaping the dynamics of international relations. These organizations serve as platforms for countries to come together and address global issues such as trade, security, and human rights. China, as one of the major players in the international arena, has a unique approach to these organizations. In this chapter, we will explore the Chinese approach to international organizations and how it aligns with their foreign policy and strategic goals.

China's involvement in international organizations has significantly increased in recent years, reflecting its growing global influence. From joining the United Nations in 1971 to becoming a founding member of the Shanghai Cooperation Organization in 2001, China has actively participated in various international organizations. This has allowed it to shape global policies and regulations to better suit its own interests.

However, China's approach to international organizations has also faced criticism. Some argue that China's actions in these organizations, such as its support for authoritarian regimes and its lack of transparency, go against the principles of international cooperation and human rights. Others argue that China's growing influence in these organizations could lead to a shift in global power dynamics, potentially causing instability and conflict.

Despite these criticisms, China's involvement in international organizations remains a crucial aspect of its foreign policy. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to these organizations will continue to shape the dynamics of international relations. In this chapter, we will delve into the key aspects of China's approach to international organizations, including its motivations, strategies, and impact on the global stage. 


## Chapter 1:5: Chinese Approach to International Organizations:




### Subsection: 14.1c Impact on International Relations

China's approach to international organizations has had a significant impact on international relations. Its principles of non-interference and mutual respect have been both praised and criticized by other countries.

On one hand, China's emphasis on non-interference has been welcomed by many developing countries, who see it as a way to protect their sovereignty and avoid external interference in their internal affairs. This has helped China to build strong relationships with these countries, particularly in Africa and Latin America.

On the other hand, China's non-interference policy has been criticized by some Western countries, who argue that it allows China to avoid accountability for its actions and to exploit the resources of other countries. This has led to tensions in the international community, particularly in issues such as human rights and environmental protection.

China's involvement in international organizations has also had a significant impact on its economic and social policies. As a member of organizations such as the WTO and the IMF, China has been subject to international rules and regulations, which have helped to shape its economic policies and practices. This has led to significant economic growth and development for China, but has also raised concerns about its trade practices and intellectual property rights.

In terms of social policies, China's involvement in organizations such as the WHO has allowed it to play a leading role in addressing global health issues. However, some critics argue that China's approach to these issues has been inconsistent, with reports of human rights abuses and censorship in the face of the COVID-19 pandemic.

In conclusion, China's approach to international organizations has had a profound impact on international relations. While it has allowed China to build strong relationships with some developing countries, it has also raised concerns and tensions with other countries. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to international organizations will continue to shape international relations and global governance.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to international organizations. We have seen how China's foreign policy is shaped by its historical and cultural background, as well as its current economic and political interests. We have also discussed the role of international organizations in China's foreign policy, and how China's involvement in these organizations has evolved over time.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that China's approach to international organizations is heavily influenced by its desire to maintain sovereignty and non-interference in its internal affairs. This has led to a cautious and selective approach to joining and participating in international organizations, with a focus on organizations that align with China's interests and values.

Furthermore, we have seen how China's involvement in international organizations has allowed it to gain a stronger voice and influence in global affairs. This has been particularly evident in recent years, as China's economic power and global influence have grown. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to international organizations will continue to evolve and shape the future of global governance.

## Chapter: Chinese Foreign Policy: International Relations and Strategy

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, international organizations play a crucial role in shaping the dynamics of international relations. These organizations serve as platforms for countries to come together and address global issues such as economic development, security, and human rights. China, as one of the major players in the international arena, has a unique approach to these organizations. In this chapter, we will explore the Chinese approach to international organizations and how it aligns with their foreign policy and strategic goals.

China's involvement in international organizations has significantly increased in recent years, reflecting its growing global influence. From joining the United Nations in 1971 to becoming a founding member of the Shanghai Cooperation Organization in 2001, China has actively participated in various international organizations. This chapter will delve into the reasons behind China's increased involvement and its impact on the global stage.

Furthermore, we will also examine the Chinese approach to international organizations, which is guided by their foreign policy and strategic goals. China's foreign policy is based on the principle of non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries and promoting economic development. We will explore how this principle shapes China's approach to international organizations and its impact on global issues.

Lastly, this chapter will also discuss the challenges and opportunities that China's involvement in international organizations presents. As China's global influence continues to grow, it faces increasing scrutiny and criticism from other countries. We will analyze how China navigates these challenges and utilizes international organizations to achieve its strategic goals.

In conclusion, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the Chinese approach to international organizations. By examining China's involvement, foreign policy, and challenges, we can gain insights into how China shapes global dynamics and its impact on the international community. 


## Chapter 15: Chinese Approach to International Organizations:




### Subsection: 14.2a Chinese Role in the UN

China's role in the United Nations (UN) has been a significant aspect of its foreign policy. As a permanent member of the UN Security Council, China has played a crucial role in shaping global policies and addressing international issues.

#### 14.2a Chinese Role in the UN

China's involvement in the UN dates back to its founding in 1945. As one of the five permanent members of the Security Council, China has been a key player in the organization's decision-making processes. Its role has been characterized by a balance between asserting its own interests and upholding the principles of non-interference and mutual respect.

One of the most significant contributions of China to the UN has been its economic support. China has been a major contributor to the UN budget, providing over $1 billion annually. This has allowed the UN to carry out its work effectively, particularly in developing countries.

China's role in the UN has also been marked by its commitment to global peace and security. As a permanent member of the Security Council, China has been involved in numerous peacekeeping missions, contributing troops and resources to maintain international peace and stability.

However, China's role in the UN has not been without controversy. Its stance on issues such as human rights and Tibet has been a source of tension with other member states. China's reluctance to criticize other countries, particularly its close ally North Korea, has also been a point of contention.

Despite these challenges, China's role in the UN has been instrumental in shaping global policies and addressing international issues. Its economic contributions and commitment to global peace and security have been crucial in maintaining the UN's effectiveness. As China continues to rise as a global power, its role in the UN is likely to become even more significant.





#### 14.2b Chinese Role in the WTO

China's role in the World Trade Organization (WTO) has been a crucial aspect of its foreign policy. As the world's largest trading nation, China's involvement in the WTO has had a significant impact on global trade and economic policies.

## Background

China's relationship with the WTO dates back to the 1980s when it began to open its economy and work towards joining the organization. However, its application for membership was met with resistance from the United States, European countries, and Japan, who demanded that China reform its tariff policies and open its markets before being admitted. This led to a lengthy negotiation process that lasted over a decade.

## Preparations

In preparation for its WTO membership, China undertook significant economic reforms. This included selling off or merging unprofitable state-owned enterprises and reforming the State Council to increase the mandate of the State Economic and Trade Commission. These reforms were crucial in aligning China's economy with the principles of the WTO.

## Membership and Impact

China became a member of the WTO on 11 December 2001, after the agreement of the Ministerial Conference. Its membership has had a significant impact on global trade and economic policies. China's large market and growing economic power have allowed it to shape global trade rules and policies. Its involvement in the WTO has also led to increased trade and investment opportunities for Chinese companies, contributing to its economic growth.

## Challenges and Controversies

Despite its significant contributions to the WTO, China's membership has also faced challenges and controversies. One of the main challenges has been enforcing compliance with WTO rules and policies. China's noncompliance with certain trade practices, such as intellectual property rights, has been a source of tension with other WTO members. This has led to disputes and negotiations, with some arguing that China's noncompliance creates benefits for its own economy.

## Conclusion

China's role in the WTO has been a crucial aspect of its foreign policy. Its membership has had a significant impact on global trade and economic policies, and its involvement has allowed it to shape global trade rules and policies. However, challenges and controversies have also arisen, highlighting the complex nature of China's relationship with the WTO. As China continues to play a significant role in the global economy, its role in the WTO will continue to be a crucial aspect of its foreign policy.





#### 14.2c Chinese Role in the WHO

China's involvement in the World Health Organization (WHO) has been a crucial aspect of its foreign policy, particularly in the areas of public health and global health governance. As the world's largest population, China's role in the WHO has had a significant impact on global health policies and initiatives.

## Background

China's relationship with the WHO dates back to the 1940s when it became a member of the organization. However, its involvement has been marked by periods of tension and controversy, particularly in the areas of public health and human rights.

## Preparations

In preparation for its role in the WHO, China has made significant investments in its public health infrastructure. This includes the construction of modern hospitals, the training of healthcare professionals, and the implementation of public health policies. China has also been a major contributor to the WHO's budget, reflecting its commitment to global health governance.

## Membership and Impact

China's membership in the WHO has had a significant impact on global health policies and initiatives. As a major contributor to the WHO's budget, China has been able to shape global health policies and initiatives. Its involvement has also been crucial in addressing global health challenges such as the SARS outbreak in 2003 and the current COVID-19 pandemic.

## Challenges and Controversies

Despite its significant contributions to the WHO, China's membership has faced challenges and controversies. One of the main challenges has been its handling of public health issues, particularly in the areas of HIV/AIDS and tuberculosis. Critics argue that China's approach to these issues has been inadequate and discriminatory, leading to international condemnation.

## Conclusion

China's role in the WHO has been a complex and evolving one. Its involvement has been marked by periods of tension and controversy, but also significant contributions to global health policies and initiatives. As China continues to play a major role in global health governance, it will be crucial for the WHO to address these challenges and controversies in order to ensure the health and well-being of all its members.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to international organizations. We have seen how China's involvement in these organizations has evolved over time, from a passive observer to an active participant. We have also discussed the various factors that have influenced China's approach, including its economic growth, political ideology, and global power dynamics.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that China's approach to international organizations is shaped by its own interests and priorities. As a rising global power, China has become increasingly assertive in its involvement in these organizations, seeking to promote its own agenda and protect its own interests. This has led to some tensions with other major powers, particularly the United States, but also opportunities for cooperation and collaboration.

Another important aspect of China's approach is its emphasis on non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries. This principle has been a cornerstone of China's foreign policy for decades, and it continues to guide its approach to international organizations. However, as China's global influence grows, it is facing increasing pressure to live up to its commitments and address issues such as human rights and environmental protection.

In conclusion, China's approach to international organizations is complex and constantly evolving. As China continues to rise as a global power, its involvement in these organizations will continue to shape the international landscape.

## Chapter: Chinese Foreign Policy: International Relations and Strategy

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, international organizations play a crucial role in shaping the dynamics of international relations. These organizations serve as platforms for countries to come together and address global issues such as economic development, security, and human rights. China, as one of the major players in the international arena, has a unique approach to these organizations. In this chapter, we will explore the Chinese approach to international organizations and how it aligns with their foreign policy and strategic objectives.

China's involvement in international organizations has been a topic of interest for many years. As the world's most populous country and second-largest economy, China's actions and decisions have a significant impact on the global stage. In recent years, China's rise as a major economic and military power has led to a shift in its approach to international organizations. This chapter will delve into the historical context of China's involvement in these organizations and how it has evolved over time.

Furthermore, we will examine the key principles and objectives that guide China's approach to international organizations. These include the concept of non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries, promoting economic development, and safeguarding its national interests. We will also discuss how China's approach aligns with its broader foreign policy goals, such as promoting a peaceful rise and becoming a responsible global power.

Finally, we will analyze the challenges and opportunities that China's approach to international organizations presents for the rest of the world. As China's influence continues to grow, it is essential to understand how its actions and decisions will shape the future of international relations. This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the Chinese approach to international organizations and its implications for the global community.


# Chinese Foreign Policy: International Relations and Strategy

## Chapter 15: Chinese Approach to International Organizations




### Conclusion

China's approach to international organizations has been a topic of great interest and debate in the international community. As one of the world's largest and most influential countries, China's actions and policies have a significant impact on global affairs. In this chapter, we have explored the various aspects of China's approach to international organizations, including its historical context, key principles and strategies, and current challenges and opportunities.

China's approach to international organizations has been shaped by its unique history and cultural values. The country's long history of isolation and self-sufficiency has led to a strong sense of national identity and a desire to maintain sovereignty and non-interference in its internal affairs. This has influenced China's approach to international organizations, as it has been cautious in joining and participating in these organizations.

However, as China's economic and political power has grown, it has become increasingly involved in international organizations. This has allowed it to play a more active role in shaping global policies and addressing global challenges. China's approach to international organizations has also been shaped by its desire to promote its own interests and values, such as non-interference and economic development.

Despite these efforts, China still faces challenges in its approach to international organizations. Its authoritarian political system and human rights record have been a source of criticism and tension with other countries. Additionally, China's growing economic and military power has raised concerns among other major powers, leading to increased scrutiny and potential conflicts.

In conclusion, China's approach to international organizations has been shaped by its unique history, cultural values, and growing global influence. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to international organizations will continue to evolve and shape global affairs.

In this chapter, we have explored the various aspects of China's approach to international organizations, including its historical context, key principles and strategies, and current challenges and opportunities.

China's approach to international organizations has been shaped by its unique history and cultural values. The country's long history of isolation and self-sufficiency has led to a strong sense of national identity and a desire to maintain sovereignty and non-interference in its internal affairs. This has influenced China's approach to international organizations, as it has been cautious in joining and participating in these organizations.

However, as China's economic and political power has grown, it has become increasingly involved in international organizations. This has allowed it to play a more active role in shaping global policies and addressing global challenges. China's approach to international organizations has also been shaped by its desire to promote its own interests and values, such as non-interference and economic development.

Despite these efforts, China still faces challenges in its approach to international organizations. Its authoritarian political system and human rights record have been a source of criticism and tension with other countries. Additionally, China's growing economic and military power has raised concerns among other major powers, leading to increased scrutiny and potential conflicts.

In conclusion, China's approach to international organizations has been shaped by its unique history, cultural values, and growing global influence. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to international organizations will continue to evolve and shape global affairs.

## Chapter 1:4: Chinese Approach to International Organizations:




### Introduction

China's foreign policy has been a topic of great interest and debate among scholars and policymakers alike. As one of the world's major powers, China's approach to international relations and strategy has significant implications for global politics. In this chapter, we will delve into the Chinese approach to non-state actors, a crucial aspect of their foreign policy.

Non-state actors, also known as non-governmental organizations (NGOs), play a significant role in international relations. They are entities that operate independently of any government and often have a specific agenda or goal. China's approach to non-state actors is shaped by its broader foreign policy objectives, including maintaining sovereignty, promoting economic development, and safeguarding its national interests.

China's engagement with non-state actors has evolved over time. In the past, China's approach was characterized by suspicion and caution, reflecting its historical experience of foreign interference. However, in recent years, China has adopted a more proactive and cooperative stance towards non-state actors. This shift is driven by China's growing global influence and its desire to shape international norms and rules.

This chapter will explore the key factors that influence China's approach to non-state actors, including its historical experience, domestic politics, and international environment. We will also examine China's engagement with specific types of non-state actors, such as multinational corporations, non-governmental organizations, and terrorist groups.

Understanding China's approach to non-state actors is crucial for comprehending its foreign policy. It provides insights into China's values, interests, and capabilities, and how it interacts with the rest of the world. This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive analysis of China's approach to non-state actors, shedding light on its motivations, strategies, and implications for global politics.




### Subsection: 15.1a Role of Non-State Actors in Foreign Policy

Non-state actors (NSAs) play a crucial role in Chinese foreign policy. As China's global influence continues to grow, its engagement with NSAs has become increasingly important. This section will explore the role of NSAs in Chinese foreign policy, focusing on their impact on China's international relations and strategy.

#### 15.1a.1 Non-State Actors and International Relations

NSAs have a significant impact on China's international relations. They are often the first point of contact for China in many countries, particularly in developing nations. NSAs, such as non-governmental organizations (NGOs), multinational corporations (MNCs), and religious groups, can provide valuable insights into local conditions and help China navigate complex political and social landscapes.

Moreover, NSAs can also serve as a bridge between China and other countries. For instance, NGOs can facilitate people-to-people exchanges and promote understanding between China and other nations. Similarly, MNCs can help China gain access to global markets and technology, contributing to its economic development.

However, NSAs can also pose challenges for China's foreign policy. For example, some NSAs may have agendas that are at odds with China's interests. In such cases, China may need to balance its engagement with these NSAs against its broader foreign policy objectives.

#### 15.1a.2 Non-State Actors and Strategy

NSAs also play a crucial role in China's strategy. They can provide valuable information and insights that can inform China's decision-making. For instance, NGOs can provide information on human rights conditions in other countries, which can be used to shape China's human rights policy. Similarly, MNCs can provide insights into global market trends, helping China to develop its economic strategy.

Furthermore, NSAs can also serve as partners in China's strategy. For example, NGOs can work with China to address global issues, such as climate change or poverty, contributing to China's image as a responsible global power. Similarly, MNCs can help China to promote its economic interests abroad, contributing to its economic growth.

However, engaging with NSAs can also pose risks for China's strategy. For instance, China's engagement with NSAs can be used by other countries to criticize China's human rights record or economic practices. Therefore, China needs to carefully manage its engagement with NSAs to ensure that it does not undermine its strategic objectives.

In conclusion, NSAs play a crucial role in Chinese foreign policy. They are important partners in China's international relations and strategy, providing valuable insights and helping to shape China's global image. However, engaging with NSAs also poses challenges that China needs to navigate carefully.




### Subsection: 15.1b Chinese Approach to Non-State Actors

China's approach to non-state actors (NSAs) is shaped by its foreign policy objectives and strategic considerations. China's engagement with NSAs is guided by the principle of non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries, which is a cornerstone of its foreign policy. This principle is reflected in China's approach to NSAs, which is characterized by a preference for bilateral relations and a reluctance to engage in multilateral initiatives.

#### 15.1b.1 Bilateralism and Non-Interference

China's preference for bilateral relations is a reflection of its non-interference policy. China believes that each country has the right to choose its own political system and development path. This principle is reflected in China's approach to NSAs, which is characterized by a preference for one-on-one relationships. This approach allows China to avoid taking positions on issues that may be contentious among NSAs, thereby avoiding potential conflicts.

However, China's non-interference policy has been criticized for allowing human rights abuses and other violations to go unchecked. For instance, China's relationship with Sudan, which has been accused of genocide in Darfur, has been a source of controversy. Similarly, China's relationship with Zimbabwe, which has been accused of human rights violations, has been a subject of criticism.

#### 15.1b.2 Multilateralism and Non-State Actors

Despite its preference for bilateral relations, China has been increasingly engaging with NSAs through multilateral initiatives. This shift reflects China's growing global influence and its desire to play a more prominent role in international affairs. For instance, China has been actively participating in the United Nations and other international organizations, where it has been advocating for a more prominent role for developing countries.

China's engagement with NSAs through multilateral initiatives has been driven by its economic interests. As China's economy continues to grow, it has become increasingly dependent on global markets and resources. This has led China to engage with NSAs, such as multinational corporations and non-governmental organizations, in a more proactive manner.

However, China's engagement with NSAs through multilateral initiatives has also been met with criticism. Some have raised concerns about China's human rights record and its treatment of NSAs, particularly in the context of its Belt and Road Initiative. These concerns have led to calls for greater transparency and accountability in China's engagement with NSAs.

In conclusion, China's approach to NSAs is shaped by its foreign policy objectives and strategic considerations. While China's non-interference policy continues to guide its approach to NSAs, its growing global influence has led it to engage with NSAs through multilateral initiatives. This shift reflects China's desire to play a more prominent role in international affairs, but it has also raised concerns about its human rights record and treatment of NSAs.




### Subsection: 15.1c Impact on International Relations

China's approach to non-state actors has had a profound impact on international relations. Its non-interference policy has been a source of controversy, with some countries accusing China of using this policy to avoid accountability for human rights abuses and other violations. However, China argues that its non-interference policy is a reflection of its respect for the sovereignty of other nations.

#### 15.1c.1 China's Non-Interference Policy and International Relations

China's non-interference policy has been a key factor in shaping its international relations. This policy has been particularly contentious in the African continent, where China has been accused of using its economic influence to avoid criticism of its human rights record. For instance, China's relationship with Sudan, which has been accused of genocide in Darfur, has been a source of controversy. Similarly, China's relationship with Zimbabwe, which has been accused of human rights violations, has been a subject of criticism.

However, China argues that its non-interference policy is a reflection of its respect for the sovereignty of other nations. It argues that each country has the right to choose its own political system and development path, and that it is not China's place to interfere in these matters. This argument has been particularly resonant in developing countries, where many see China as a model of economic development that they can emulate without having to adopt Western political systems.

#### 15.1c.2 China's Engagement with Non-State Actors and International Relations

Despite its non-interference policy, China has been increasingly engaging with non-state actors through multilateral initiatives. This shift reflects China's growing global influence and its desire to play a more prominent role in international affairs. For instance, China has been actively participating in the United Nations and other international organizations, where it has been advocating for a more prominent role for developing countries.

China's engagement with non-state actors through multilateral initiatives has been driven by its desire to promote its own interests and to shape international norms and rules in a way that is favorable to it. For instance, China has been advocating for a more prominent role for developing countries in international organizations, arguing that this is necessary to ensure that the interests of these countries are adequately represented. This has been particularly evident in China's engagement with the United Nations, where it has been pushing for reforms that would increase the representation of developing countries.

In conclusion, China's approach to non-state actors has had a profound impact on international relations. Its non-interference policy has been a source of controversy, but its engagement with non-state actors through multilateral initiatives has been a reflection of its growing global influence. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to non-state actors will continue to shape international relations in significant ways.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have delved into the Chinese approach to non-state actors, a critical aspect of Chinese foreign policy. We have explored how China's approach to non-state actors is shaped by its historical, cultural, and political background. The Chinese approach to non-state actors is characterized by a careful balance of engagement and control, reflecting China's desire to maintain its sovereignty and promote its interests while also managing potential threats.

China's approach to non-state actors is also influenced by its economic interests. As China's economic power continues to grow, it has become increasingly engaged with non-state actors, particularly in the African continent. This engagement has been driven by China's desire to secure access to natural resources and to promote its economic interests.

However, China's approach to non-state actors is not without challenges. The rise of non-state actors has posed new threats to China's security, including the risk of terrorism and the spread of radical ideologies. China's approach to these threats has been characterized by a combination of military and diplomatic efforts, reflecting China's desire to maintain its security while also managing its international image.

In conclusion, China's approach to non-state actors is a complex and evolving aspect of Chinese foreign policy. It reflects China's historical, cultural, and political background, as well as its economic interests and security concerns. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to non-state actors will continue to evolve and shape international relations.

## Chapter: Chapter 16: Chinese Approach to International Organizations

### Introduction

The Chinese approach to international organizations is a critical aspect of Chinese foreign policy. As China continues to rise as a global power, its engagement with international organizations has become increasingly important. This chapter will delve into the Chinese approach to international organizations, exploring the historical, cultural, and political factors that shape this approach.

China's engagement with international organizations has evolved significantly over time. From its early days as a non-permanent member of the United Nations Security Council to its current status as a permanent member, China's approach to international organizations has been shaped by its desire to maintain its sovereignty and promote its interests. This chapter will explore how China's approach to international organizations has evolved over time, and the factors that have influenced this evolution.

The Chinese approach to international organizations is also shaped by its economic interests. As China's economic power continues to grow, it has become increasingly engaged with international organizations, particularly those related to trade and economic development. This chapter will examine how China's economic interests have influenced its approach to international organizations, and the challenges and opportunities this has presented.

Finally, this chapter will explore the challenges and opportunities presented by China's approach to international organizations. As China's economic and political power continues to grow, its approach to international organizations will continue to shape global politics and economics. This chapter will examine the implications of China's approach to international organizations for the rest of the world, and the opportunities and challenges this presents for other countries.

In conclusion, this chapter will provide a comprehensive analysis of the Chinese approach to international organizations, exploring the historical, cultural, and political factors that shape this approach, and the challenges and opportunities this presents for the rest of the world.




### Subsection: 15.2a Chinese Approach to NGOs

China's approach to non-governmental organizations (NGOs) has been shaped by its broader foreign policy objectives, particularly its desire to maintain sovereignty and control over its own affairs. This approach has been characterized by a mix of cooperation and caution, with China often working closely with NGOs on issues of mutual concern, while also maintaining strict controls over their activities.

#### 15.2a.1 China's Engagement with NGOs

China's engagement with NGOs has been guided by its non-interference policy. This policy, which emphasizes respect for the sovereignty of other nations, has been a key factor in shaping China's approach to NGOs. China has been particularly cautious in its engagement with NGOs that operate in areas that it considers to be of strategic importance, such as human rights and religious freedom.

Despite this caution, China has been increasingly engaging with NGOs in recent years. This engagement has been driven by a variety of factors, including China's growing economic power, its desire to improve its international image, and its recognition of the role that NGOs can play in addressing domestic and global challenges.

#### 15.2a.2 China's Control over NGOs

Despite its increasing engagement with NGOs, China maintains strict controls over their activities. This is reflected in the three laws that were implemented in the 1980s and 1990s to regulate NGOs: the Regulations on the Registration and Management of Social Organizations, the Regulations on the Registration and Management of Foundations, and the Interim Provisions for the Administration of Foreign Chambers of Commerce in China.

These laws require NGOs to register with the government and obtain approval for their activities. They also impose restrictions on the types of activities that NGOs can undertake, particularly those that relate to human rights and religious freedom. NGOs that operate without registration or approval can face severe penalties, including fines and imprisonment.

#### 15.2a.3 China's Impact on NGOs

China's approach to NGOs has had a significant impact on the work of these organizations. On one hand, China's increasing engagement with NGOs has provided opportunities for these organizations to contribute to the resolution of domestic and global challenges. On the other hand, China's strict controls over NGOs have limited their ability to operate freely and have raised concerns about their independence and effectiveness.

In conclusion, China's approach to NGOs reflects its broader foreign policy objectives, particularly its desire to maintain sovereignty and control over its own affairs. While China's engagement with NGOs has been increasing, its strict controls over these organizations have raised concerns about their independence and effectiveness.




### Subsection: 15.2b Chinese Approach to Multinational Corporations

China's approach to multinational corporations (MNCs) has been shaped by its broader economic policy objectives, particularly its desire to promote economic growth and modernization. This approach has been characterized by a mix of cooperation and competition, with China often working closely with MNCs on issues of mutual concern, while also maintaining strict controls over their activities.

#### 15.2b.1 China's Engagement with MNCs

China's engagement with MNCs has been guided by its non-interference policy. This policy, which emphasizes respect for the sovereignty of other nations, has been a key factor in shaping China's approach to MNCs. China has been particularly cautious in its engagement with MNCs that operate in areas that it considers to be of strategic importance, such as telecommunications and energy.

Despite this caution, China has been increasingly engaging with MNCs in recent years. This engagement has been driven by a variety of factors, including China's growing economic power, its desire to improve its international image, and its recognition of the role that MNCs can play in modernizing its economy.

#### 15.2b.2 China's Control over MNCs

Despite its increasing engagement with MNCs, China maintains strict controls over their activities. This is reflected in the three laws that were implemented in the 1980s and 1990s to regulate MNCs: the Regulations on the Registration and Management of Foreign-Invested Enterprises, the Regulations on the Registration and Management of Foreign-Invested Enterprises (Amended), and the Regulations on the Registration and Management of Foreign-Invested Enterprises (Amended).

These laws require MNCs to register with the government and obtain approval for their activities. They also impose restrictions on the types of activities that MNCs can undertake, particularly those that relate to sensitive industries or technologies. MNCs that operate without registration or approval can face severe penalties, including fines and imprisonment.

#### 15.2b.3 China's Approach to MNCs in the Belt and Road Initiative

The Belt and Road Initiative (BRI), launched by China in 2013, has been a key driver of China's engagement with MNCs. The BRI aims to enhance connectivity and cooperation between China and other countries, and MNCs play a crucial role in this process.

China's approach to MNCs in the BRI has been characterized by a mix of cooperation and competition. On the one hand, China has been working closely with MNCs to implement BRI projects, providing them with favorable policies and incentives. On the other hand, China has also been competing with other countries for MNCs' investment and participation in the BRI.

Despite these challenges, China's approach to MNCs in the BRI has been largely successful. MNCs have been actively involved in BRI projects, contributing to the modernization of China's economy and infrastructure. This engagement has not only benefited China but also other BRI countries, which have been able to attract much-needed investment and technology.

In conclusion, China's approach to MNCs has been shaped by its broader economic and foreign policy objectives. Despite strict controls, China has been increasingly engaging with MNCs, recognizing their potential to drive economic growth and modernization. The BRI has been a key driver of this engagement, providing a platform for cooperation and competition between China and MNCs.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to non-state actors, focusing on their interactions with multinational corporations (MNCs). We have seen how China's foreign policy towards MNCs has evolved over time, from a policy of non-interference to a more proactive approach that includes cooperation and competition. We have also examined the factors that have influenced this evolution, including China's economic growth, its increasing global influence, and the changing nature of MNCs themselves.

China's approach to MNCs is a complex and multifaceted one, reflecting its broader foreign policy objectives. On one hand, China seeks to attract MNCs to its market, which provides a source of technology, investment, and job creation. On the other hand, China also seeks to protect its own industries and promote its own companies, both domestically and internationally. This has led to a mix of cooperation and competition in China's interactions with MNCs.

Despite these complexities, China's approach to MNCs has been largely successful. China's economic growth has been fueled in part by the influx of MNCs, and Chinese companies have become major players in global markets. However, there are also challenges and risks associated with this approach, including concerns about intellectual property rights, market access, and the impact of MNCs on local industries.

In conclusion, China's approach to non-state actors, particularly MNCs, is a critical aspect of its foreign policy. It reflects China's economic and political objectives, and its interactions with MNCs have had a significant impact on China's development and its role in the global economy.

#### Exercise 2

#### Exercise 3

#### Exercise 4

## Chapter: Chapter 16: Chinese Approach to International Organizations

### Introduction

The Chinese approach to international organizations is a critical aspect of its foreign policy. As a rising global power, China's interactions with international organizations have significant implications for the international community. This chapter will delve into the Chinese approach to international organizations, exploring the principles, strategies, and policies that guide China's participation in these organizations.

China's approach to international organizations is shaped by its unique historical, cultural, and political background. The country's long history of isolation and its subsequent rapid modernization have influenced its approach to international organizations. China's rise as a global power has also led to a shift in its foreign policy, with a greater emphasis on international cooperation and participation in international organizations.

This chapter will also examine the role of international organizations in China's foreign policy. China's participation in these organizations has allowed it to play a more active role in global affairs, shaping international norms and policies. The chapter will also discuss the challenges and opportunities that China's participation in international organizations presents for the global community.

In addition, this chapter will explore the impact of China's approach to international organizations on its relations with other countries. China's approach to international organizations has been a key factor in its relations with other major powers, including the United States and European Union. The chapter will also discuss how China's approach to international organizations has influenced its relations with developing countries.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the Chinese approach to international organizations. It will shed light on the principles, strategies, and policies that guide China's participation in these organizations, and the implications of this approach for the global community.




### Subsection: 15.2c Chinese Approach to Terrorist Groups

China's approach to terrorist groups has been shaped by its broader foreign policy objectives, particularly its desire to maintain stability and protect its national interests. This approach has been characterized by a mix of cooperation and competition, with China often working closely with other countries to combat terrorism, while also maintaining strict controls over its own territory.

#### 15.2c.1 China's Engagement with Terrorist Groups

China's engagement with terrorist groups has been guided by its non-interference policy. This policy, which emphasizes respect for the sovereignty of other nations, has been a key factor in shaping China's approach to terrorist groups. China has been particularly cautious in its engagement with terrorist groups that operate in areas that it considers to be of strategic importance, such as Xinjiang and Tibet.

Despite this caution, China has been increasingly engaging with other countries to combat terrorism. This engagement has been driven by a variety of factors, including China's growing economic power, its desire to improve its international image, and its recognition of the threat that terrorist groups pose to its national security.

#### 15.2c.2 China's Control over Terrorist Groups

Despite its increasing engagement with other countries to combat terrorism, China maintains strict controls over its own territory. This is reflected in the various laws and regulations that China has implemented to combat terrorism, including the Anti-Terrorism Law of the People's Republic of China and the Regulations on the Administration of Activities of Overseas Non-Governmental Organizations within the Territory of China.

These laws and regulations impose strict controls on the activities of terrorist groups within China, including restrictions on their ability to operate, recruit, and fundraise. They also provide for harsh penalties for those found guilty of terrorist offenses, including life imprisonment or the death penalty.

#### 15.2c.3 China's Approach to Terrorist Groups

China's approach to terrorist groups is characterized by a mix of cooperation and competition. On the one hand, China works closely with other countries to combat terrorism, sharing intelligence and coordinating efforts to disrupt and dismantle terrorist groups. On the other hand, China maintains strict controls over its own territory, using a combination of legal and extra-legal measures to prevent and respond to terrorist threats.

This approach reflects China's broader foreign policy objectives, particularly its desire to maintain stability and protect its national interests. It also reflects China's commitment to the principles of non-interference and respect for sovereignty, which guide its engagement with other countries on issues of terrorism and security.




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to non-state actors, specifically focusing on their relationship with the United States. We have seen how China's foreign policy towards non-state actors has evolved over time, from a policy of non-interference to a more proactive approach. This evolution has been driven by China's growing economic and political power, as well as its desire to secure its national interests.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that China's approach to non-state actors is heavily influenced by its relationship with the United States. As the world's largest economy and a global superpower, the United States plays a crucial role in shaping China's foreign policy. China's desire to be seen as a responsible global power has led it to adopt a more cooperative approach towards non-state actors, particularly in the areas of trade and investment.

However, China's relationship with the United States is not without its challenges. The two countries have significant differences in their approaches to non-state actors, with the United States taking a more interventionist stance. This has led to tensions and conflicts, particularly in the areas of human rights and democracy promotion.

Despite these challenges, China's approach to non-state actors has been largely successful. Its economic and political influence has grown significantly, and it has been able to secure its national interests while also maintaining its image as a responsible global power. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to non-state actors will continue to evolve and shape the dynamics of international relations.

In conclusion, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the Chinese approach to international organizations. By examining China's involvement, foreign policy, and strategic goals, we can gain insights into how China navigates the complex landscape of international relations.

## Chapter 1:6: Chinese Approach to International Organizations:




### Introduction

China's rise as a global power has been accompanied by a growing interest in global governance. As the world's most populous country and second-largest economy, China's actions and policies have a significant impact on the international community. In this chapter, we will explore the Chinese approach to global governance, examining their views on international organizations, human rights, and global economic governance.

China's approach to global governance is shaped by its unique history and culture. The country's long history of Confucianism, which emphasizes the importance of hierarchy and respect for authority, has influenced China's approach to international relations. This has led to a preference for a more hierarchical and paternalistic approach to global governance, where China plays a leading role.

In recent years, China has also become more assertive in its foreign policy, challenging the dominance of Western powers in global governance institutions. This has led to tensions with the United States and other Western powers, who view China's actions as a threat to the existing global order.

In this chapter, we will also examine the impact of China's Belt and Road Initiative (BRI) on global governance. The BRI, which aims to connect China with Europe, Africa, and other parts of the world through a network of infrastructure projects, has been criticized for its lack of transparency and potential for debt-trap diplomacy. We will explore the implications of the BRI for global governance and the challenges it poses for international organizations.

Overall, this chapter will provide a comprehensive analysis of China's approach to global governance, examining its historical roots, current policies, and future implications. By understanding China's approach to global governance, we can gain valuable insights into the country's role in shaping the future of international relations.




### Subsection: 16.1a Role of Global Governance in Foreign Policy

China's approach to global governance is shaped by its unique history and culture. The country's long history of Confucianism, which emphasizes the importance of hierarchy and respect for authority, has influenced China's approach to international relations. This has led to a preference for a more hierarchical and paternalistic approach to global governance, where China plays a leading role.

In recent years, China has also become more assertive in its foreign policy, challenging the dominance of Western powers in global governance institutions. This has led to tensions with the United States and other Western powers, who view China's actions as a threat to the existing global order.

One of the key areas where China's approach to global governance is evident is in its stance on global health governance. China's Belt and Road Initiative (BRI), which aims to connect China with Europe, Africa, and other parts of the world through a network of infrastructure projects, has been criticized for its lack of transparency and potential for debt-trap diplomacy. This has raised concerns about the impact of the BRI on global health governance, as China's actions could potentially undermine the efforts of international organizations to address global health issues.

China's approach to global health governance is also evident in its response to the COVID-19 pandemic. The Chinese government has been criticized for its handling of the initial outbreak of the virus, as well as its lack of transparency in sharing information about the virus and its origins. This has raised concerns about China's commitment to global health governance and its willingness to adhere to international norms and standards.

In addition to its actions in global health governance, China's approach to global governance is also evident in its stance on human rights. China's treatment of its Uighur minority and its crackdown on dissent have been criticized by human rights organizations and Western powers. This has led to tensions with the United States and other Western powers, who view China's actions as a violation of international human rights norms.

Overall, China's approach to global governance is shaped by its unique history and culture, as well as its growing global power. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to global governance will continue to shape international relations and have a significant impact on the global order.





### Subsection: 16.1b Chinese Approach to Global Governance

China's approach to global governance is shaped by its unique history and culture. The country's long history of Confucianism, which emphasizes the importance of hierarchy and respect for authority, has influenced China's approach to international relations. This has led to a preference for a more hierarchical and paternalistic approach to global governance, where China plays a leading role.

In recent years, China has also become more assertive in its foreign policy, challenging the dominance of Western powers in global governance institutions. This has led to tensions with the United States and other Western powers, who view China's actions as a threat to the existing global order.

One of the key areas where China's approach to global governance is evident is in its stance on global health governance. China's Belt and Road Initiative (BRI), which aims to connect China with Europe, Africa, and other parts of the world through a network of infrastructure projects, has been criticized for its lack of transparency and potential for debt-trap diplomacy. This has raised concerns about the impact of the BRI on global health governance, as China's actions could potentially undermine the efforts of international organizations to address global health issues.

China's approach to global health governance is also evident in its response to the COVID-19 pandemic. The Chinese government has been criticized for its handling of the initial outbreak of the virus, as well as its lack of transparency in sharing information about the virus and its origins. This has raised concerns about China's commitment to global health governance and its willingness to adhere to international norms and standards.

In addition to its actions in global health governance, China's approach to global governance is also evident in its stance on environmental governance. China has been a major contributor to global environmental issues, such as climate change and pollution, and has faced criticism for its lack of action in addressing these issues. However, in recent years, China has taken steps to improve its environmental policies and has become a major investor in renewable energy. This has led to tensions with the United States and other Western powers, who view China's actions as insufficient and insincere.

China's approach to global governance also extends to its stance on human rights. China has been criticized for its human rights record, particularly in regards to its treatment of ethnic minorities and religious groups. The Chinese government has also been accused of censoring and controlling information, limiting freedom of expression and dissent. This has led to tensions with the United States and other Western powers, who view China's actions as a violation of international human rights norms.

Overall, China's approach to global governance is shaped by its desire to maintain its sovereignty and promote its own interests. This has led to tensions with the United States and other Western powers, who view China's actions as a threat to the existing global order. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to global governance will continue to shape international relations and have a significant impact on the future of global governance.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to global governance. We have seen how China's rise as a global power has led to a shift in its foreign policy, with a greater emphasis on international relations and strategy. China's approach to global governance is shaped by its historical and cultural background, as well as its current economic and political interests. We have also discussed the challenges and opportunities that China's approach to global governance presents for the international community.

China's approach to global governance is characterized by a combination of cooperation and competition. On one hand, China has been actively participating in international organizations and initiatives, such as the United Nations and the World Trade Organization. On the other hand, China has also been asserting its own interests and promoting its own agenda, particularly in areas such as trade and security. This has led to tensions with other major powers, particularly the United States, and has raised questions about China's intentions and actions in the global arena.

Despite these challenges, China's approach to global governance also presents opportunities for the international community. China's economic and political power can be harnessed to address global issues, such as climate change and poverty. China's Belt and Road Initiative, for example, has the potential to boost economic development and connectivity in Eurasia and Africa. Additionally, China's emphasis on non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries aligns with the principles of sovereignty and non-intervention, which are widely accepted in the international community.

In conclusion, China's approach to global governance is complex and multifaceted. It is shaped by a combination of historical, cultural, economic, and political factors, and presents both challenges and opportunities for the international community. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to global governance will continue to evolve and shape the future of international relations.

## Chapter: Chinese Foreign Policy: International Relations and Strategy

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, the role of China in international relations has become increasingly significant. As the world's most populous country and second-largest economy, China's foreign policy decisions have a major impact on the global political and economic landscape. In this chapter, we will explore the Chinese approach to regional security, which is a crucial aspect of their foreign policy.

China's approach to regional security is shaped by its historical and cultural background, as well as its current economic and political interests. China's foreign policy is guided by the principle of non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries, which has been a cornerstone of its approach to regional security. This principle is rooted in China's own history of being subjected to foreign interference and colonization.

In recent years, China's economic and military power has allowed it to play a more assertive role in regional security. China has become a major trading partner and investor for many countries, and its growing economic influence has led to increased involvement in regional security issues. At the same time, China's military modernization and expansion have raised concerns among its neighbors and the international community.

In this chapter, we will examine the key factors that shape China's approach to regional security, including its historical and cultural background, economic interests, and military capabilities. We will also explore how China's approach to regional security has evolved over time and its impact on the international community. By understanding China's approach to regional security, we can gain valuable insights into its foreign policy decisions and their implications for the global order.

### Subsection: 16.1c Impact on International Relations

China's approach to global governance has had a significant impact on international relations. Its assertive stance and actions in global governance institutions have led to tensions with Western powers, particularly the United States. This has resulted in a power struggle between the two countries, with China seeking to challenge the dominance of Western powers in global governance and the US seeking to maintain its influence.

China's actions in global health governance have also raised concerns among other countries. Its handling of the COVID-19 pandemic and its lack of transparency in sharing information about the virus have been criticized, leading to strained relations with other countries. This has also affected China's image in the international community, with some viewing it as a threat to global health governance.

In terms of environmental governance, China's actions have also had a significant impact on international relations. As one of the major contributors to global environmental issues, its actions or lack thereof have been closely watched by other countries. Its reluctance to take strong action on climate change and its environmental policies have led to criticism and tensions with other countries, particularly those that are more environmentally conscious.

Furthermore, China's Belt and Road Initiative (BRI) has also raised concerns among other countries. Its lack of transparency and potential for debt-trap diplomacy have led to suspicions and concerns about the intentions behind the BRI. This has also affected China's relations with other countries, particularly those that are wary of its economic influence.

In conclusion, China's approach to global governance has had a significant impact on international relations. Its actions and policies have led to tensions and power struggles with Western powers, raised concerns about its commitment to global health and environmental governance, and raised suspicions about its intentions with the BRI. As China continues to assert its influence in global governance, it will be interesting to see how these tensions and power struggles play out in the future.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to global governance. We have seen how China's rise as a global power has led to a shift in its foreign policy, with a greater emphasis on international relations and strategy. China's approach to global governance is characterized by a combination of pragmatism and assertiveness, as it seeks to balance its own interests with those of the international community.

China's approach to global governance is shaped by its historical and cultural background. The country's long history of Confucianism and its emphasis on hierarchy and respect for authority have influenced its approach to international relations. This has led to a preference for a more hierarchical and paternalistic approach to global governance, where China plays a leading role.

However, China's approach to global governance has also faced criticism and challenges. Its human rights record and lack of transparency in its domestic affairs have been raised as concerns by other countries. Additionally, China's growing economic and military power has led to tensions with other major global powers, particularly the United States.

Despite these challenges, China's approach to global governance has also brought about positive changes. Its Belt and Road Initiative, for example, has been praised for its potential to boost economic development and connectivity in the global community. China's role in addressing global issues such as climate change and global health has also been recognized and appreciated by many countries.

In conclusion, China's approach to global governance is complex and multifaceted. It is shaped by its historical and cultural background, as well as its current global power status. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to global governance will continue to evolve and shape the future of international relations.

China's involvement in international organizations has significantly increased in recent years, reflecting its growing global influence. From joining the United Nations in 1971 to becoming a founding member of the Shanghai Cooperation Organization in 2001, China has actively participated in various international organizations. This chapter will delve into the reasons behind China's increased involvement and its impact on the global stage.

Furthermore, we will also examine China's approach to international organizations, which is guided by its foreign policy and strategic objectives. China's foreign policy is based on the principle of non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries, and this is reflected in its approach to international organizations. We will explore how China's foreign policy shapes its interactions with other countries within these organizations and how it uses these platforms to advance its own interests.

Lastly, this chapter will also discuss the challenges and criticisms faced by China in its involvement with international organizations.
