# Chinese Foreign Policy: International Relations and Strategy

## Chapter 19: Chinese Approach to Global Security




### Introduction

China's approach to the global economy has been a topic of great interest and debate among scholars and policymakers. As the world's second-largest economy, China's economic policies and strategies have a significant impact on the global economic landscape. In this chapter, we will explore the Chinese approach to the global economy, examining their economic policies, strategies, and their implications for the international community.

China's economic policies and strategies have evolved significantly over the years, reflecting the country's changing economic landscape and its growing global influence. From its early days as a closed and centrally planned economy, China has transformed into a major player in the global economy, with a thriving private sector and a growing middle class. This transformation has been driven by a combination of economic policies and strategies that have been carefully crafted and implemented by the Chinese government.

One of the key aspects of China's approach to the global economy is its emphasis on economic development and modernization. The Chinese government has been actively promoting economic growth and modernization through various policies and initiatives, such as the "Made in China 2025" plan and the Belt and Road Initiative. These initiatives aim to transform China into a high-tech and innovative economy, and to increase its global economic influence.

Another important aspect of China's approach to the global economy is its focus on international trade and investment. China has become a major trading power, with a significant share of global trade. The Chinese government has been actively promoting trade and investment, both domestically and internationally, through various policies and initiatives. This has not only boosted China's own economic growth, but has also had a significant impact on the global economy.

However, China's economic policies and strategies have also faced criticism and challenges. Some have raised concerns about China's trade practices, such as its currency manipulation and intellectual property rights violations. Others have questioned the sustainability of China's economic growth, given its high levels of debt and reliance on investment and exports.

In this chapter, we will delve deeper into these issues and explore the Chinese approach to the global economy in more detail. We will examine the key economic policies and strategies of China, and their implications for the international community. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of China's role in the global economy and its impact on the world.




### Subsection: 19.1a Role of Global Economy in Foreign Policy

The global economy plays a crucial role in shaping China's foreign policy. As the world's second-largest economy, China's economic policies and strategies have a significant impact on the global economic landscape. This is reflected in China's approach to the global economy, which is characterized by a combination of economic policies and strategies that aim to promote economic growth and modernization, increase global economic influence, and address domestic economic challenges.

#### Economic Policies and Strategies

China's economic policies and strategies have evolved significantly over the years, reflecting the country's changing economic landscape and its growing global influence. From its early days as a closed and centrally planned economy, China has transformed into a major player in the global economy, with a thriving private sector and a growing middle class. This transformation has been driven by a combination of economic policies and strategies that have been carefully crafted and implemented by the Chinese government.

One of the key aspects of China's approach to the global economy is its emphasis on economic development and modernization. The Chinese government has been actively promoting economic growth and modernization through various policies and initiatives, such as the "Made in China 2025" plan and the Belt and Road Initiative. These initiatives aim to transform China into a high-tech and innovative economy, and to increase its global economic influence.

Another important aspect of China's approach to the global economy is its focus on international trade and investment. China has become a major trading power, with a significant share of global trade. The Chinese government has been actively promoting trade and investment, both domestically and internationally, through various policies and initiatives. This has not only boosted China's own economic growth, but has also had a significant impact on the global economy.

#### Global Economic Challenges

Despite its economic success, China faces several global economic challenges that have a direct impact on its foreign policy. One of the main challenges is the rise of China's economic power and its potential to disrupt the global economic order. As China's economy continues to grow, it poses a threat to the dominance of Western economies and their economic policies. This has led to tensions and conflicts between China and other major economic powers, particularly the United States.

Another challenge is the issue of economic inequality within China. Despite its economic growth, there are still significant disparities in wealth and income between different regions and social groups in China. This has led to social unrest and political instability, which can have a negative impact on China's foreign policy.

#### Global Economic Impact

China's approach to the global economy has had a significant impact on the global economic landscape. Its economic policies and strategies have not only boosted its own economic growth, but have also had a ripple effect on the global economy. For example, China's Belt and Road Initiative has created new opportunities for trade and investment, not only for China, but also for other countries along the Belt and Road. This has helped to stimulate economic growth and development in these countries, and has also contributed to the overall growth of the global economy.

However, China's economic policies and strategies have also faced criticism and challenges. Some argue that China's economic policies, particularly its currency manipulation and trade practices, have contributed to global economic imbalances and have led to tensions with other major economic powers. Additionally, China's economic growth has been accompanied by environmental degradation and social inequality, which have raised concerns about the sustainability of its economic model.

In conclusion, the global economy plays a crucial role in shaping China's foreign policy. Its economic policies and strategies have had a significant impact on the global economic landscape, but have also faced challenges and criticisms. As China continues to rise as a global economic power, its approach to the global economy will continue to be a key factor in its foreign policy decisions.





### Subsection: 19.1b Chinese Approach to Global Economy

China's approach to the global economy is shaped by its unique economic policies and strategies, as well as its historical and cultural context. The Chinese government's approach to the global economy is characterized by a combination of pragmatism, strategic thinking, and a strong emphasis on economic development and modernization.

#### Pragmatism and Strategic Thinking

China's approach to the global economy is marked by a strong emphasis on pragmatism and strategic thinking. The Chinese government is known for its ability to adapt to changing economic conditions and to make strategic decisions that serve its long-term economic interests. This approach is reflected in China's economic policies and strategies, which are often characterized by a combination of short-term adjustments and long-term planning.

For example, China's response to the global financial crisis of 2008 was marked by a combination of short-term stimulus measures and long-term economic reforms. The Chinese government implemented a series of stimulus measures, including a massive infrastructure spending program, to boost economic growth and to prevent a deeper economic downturn. At the same time, it also launched a series of long-term economic reforms, such as the "Made in China 2025" plan, to promote economic modernization and to increase China's global economic influence.

#### Economic Development and Modernization

China's approach to the global economy is also characterized by a strong emphasis on economic development and modernization. The Chinese government has been actively promoting economic growth and modernization through various policies and initiatives, such as the "Made in China 2025" plan and the Belt and Road Initiative. These initiatives aim to transform China into a high-tech and innovative economy, and to increase its global economic influence.

The "Made in China 2025" plan, for example, aims to upgrade China's manufacturing sector and to transform it into a high-tech and innovative industry. This plan includes a series of initiatives, such as the promotion of advanced manufacturing technologies, the development of a domestic supply chain, and the training of a skilled workforce. The Belt and Road Initiative, on the other hand, aims to increase China's global economic influence by promoting infrastructure development and economic cooperation along the ancient Silk Road routes.

#### Addressing Domestic Economic Challenges

Finally, China's approach to the global economy also involves addressing domestic economic challenges. China's economy is facing a number of challenges, including a slowing growth rate, a rising debt level, and a widening income gap. The Chinese government has been actively addressing these challenges through various economic policies and strategies.

For example, the Chinese government has been implementing a series of measures to address the slowing growth rate. These measures include a series of stimulus measures, such as a massive infrastructure spending program, as well as long-term economic reforms, such as the "Made in China 2025" plan. The Chinese government has also been implementing policies to address the rising debt level, such as a crackdown on shadow banking and a push for deleveraging. Finally, the Chinese government has been implementing policies to address the widening income gap, such as a minimum wage increase and a push for income redistribution.

In conclusion, China's approach to the global economy is shaped by its unique economic policies and strategies, as well as its historical and cultural context. The Chinese government's approach to the global economy is characterized by a combination of pragmatism, strategic thinking, and a strong emphasis on economic development and modernization. This approach has allowed China to become a major player in the global economy, and has enabled it to address its domestic economic challenges.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to the global economy. We have seen how China's economic policies and strategies have evolved over time, from a closed and centrally planned economy to a more open and market-oriented one. We have also examined the role of China in the global economy, as a major trading partner and investor for many countries.

China's approach to the global economy is characterized by a combination of pragmatism and strategic thinking. The Chinese government has been able to navigate the complexities of the global economy by adopting a flexible and adaptive approach. This has allowed China to maintain its economic growth and stability, even in the face of global economic challenges.

Furthermore, China's economic policies and strategies have had a significant impact on the global economy. Its rapid economic growth has created new opportunities for other countries, particularly in terms of trade and investment. However, it has also raised concerns about China's economic dominance and its impact on global trade and economic stability.

In conclusion, China's approach to the global economy is a crucial aspect of its foreign policy. It has allowed China to become a major player in the global economy, while also facing challenges and criticisms. As China continues to rise as a global economic power, its approach to the global economy will continue to shape the dynamics of the international economic landscape.

## Chapter: Chapter 20: Chinese Approach to Global Security

### Introduction

The Chinese approach to global security is a critical aspect of its foreign policy. As one of the world's major powers, China's stance on global security has significant implications for the international community. This chapter will delve into the Chinese perspective on global security, exploring its historical context, key principles, and current strategies.

China's approach to global security is shaped by its unique historical and cultural background. The country's long history of Confucian philosophy, which emphasizes harmony and non-confrontation, has influenced its approach to international relations. This has led to a preference for peaceful coexistence and non-interference in the internal affairs of other nations.

In recent years, China's economic growth and increasing global influence have necessitated a more active role in global security affairs. The Chinese government has been advocating for a more equitable and inclusive global security architecture, emphasizing the importance of mutual respect and cooperation among nations.

This chapter will also examine China's current security strategies, including its approach to issues such as terrorism, nuclear proliferation, and cyber security. It will also discuss the challenges and opportunities that China's rise presents for global security, and how these are shaping its foreign policy decisions.

By understanding the Chinese approach to global security, we can gain valuable insights into the country's foreign policy and its role in the international community. This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive overview of this complex and evolving topic, shedding light on China's perspective on global security and its implications for the world.




### Subsection: 19.1c Impact on International Relations

China's approach to the global economy has had a profound impact on international relations. Its economic policies and strategies have not only influenced the global economic landscape but have also shaped its relationships with other countries.

#### Economic Power and Influence

China's economic power and influence have been growing rapidly in recent years. As the world's second-largest economy, China's economic decisions have a significant impact on the global economy. Its economic policies, such as the "Made in China 2025" plan and the Belt and Road Initiative, have been met with both admiration and criticism from other countries.

The "Made in China 2025" plan, for example, has been seen as a threat by some countries, particularly the United States, due to its focus on high-tech industries and its potential to further increase China's economic dominance. On the other hand, the Belt and Road Initiative, with its massive infrastructure investments, has been welcomed by many developing countries as a source of much-needed funding and development.

#### Economic Diplomacy

China's economic policies and strategies have also been used as a tool for economic diplomacy. The Chinese government has been actively promoting its economic initiatives, such as the Belt and Road Initiative, as a means of enhancing its global influence and strengthening its relationships with other countries.

For instance, China's economic investments in Africa have been seen as a way to gain access to natural resources and to increase its influence in the region. Similarly, its economic initiatives in Latin America have been viewed as a means of countering the influence of the United States in the region.

#### Economic Conflict

Despite its economic power and influence, China's approach to the global economy has also led to economic conflicts with other countries. The United States, in particular, has been critical of China's economic policies, accusing it of unfair trade practices and intellectual property theft.

The US-China trade imbalance, for example, has been a major source of economic conflict between the two countries. The US has been pressing China to reduce its trade surplus with the US, arguing that it is a result of unfair trade practices, such as currency manipulation and intellectual property theft.

In conclusion, China's approach to the global economy has had a significant impact on international relations. Its economic power and influence, economic diplomacy, and economic conflicts have all shaped its relationships with other countries. As China continues to rise as a global economic power, its approach to the global economy will continue to be a key factor in international relations.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to the global economy. We have seen how China's economic policies and strategies have evolved over time, from a closed and centrally planned economy to a more open and market-oriented one. We have also examined the role of China in the global economy, as a major trading partner and investor for many countries.

China's approach to the global economy is characterized by a combination of pragmatism and strategic thinking. The Chinese government has been able to navigate the complexities of the global economy, adapting to changes and challenges as they arise. This has allowed China to maintain a high rate of economic growth and to become a major player in the global economic landscape.

However, China's approach to the global economy is not without its challenges. The country faces significant economic challenges, including a slowing rate of economic growth, rising debt levels, and increasing income inequality. These challenges will require the Chinese government to continue to adapt and evolve its economic policies and strategies.

In conclusion, the Chinese approach to the global economy is a complex and dynamic one. It is shaped by a variety of factors, including the country's history, culture, and political system. As China continues to rise as a global power, its approach to the global economy will continue to be a key factor in shaping international relations and global economic dynamics.

## Chapter: Chapter 20: Chinese Approach to Global Security

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the Chinese approach to global security. China's foreign policy has been a topic of great interest and debate among scholars and policymakers alike. Its rise as a global power has been accompanied by a shift in its foreign policy, particularly in the realm of security. As China's economic and military power continues to grow, its approach to global security has become a critical factor in international relations.

China's approach to global security is shaped by its unique historical, cultural, and political background. The country's long history of Confucian philosophy, which emphasizes harmony and non-confrontation, has influenced its approach to security. This has been further shaped by its experience with imperialism and colonialism, which has led to a deep-seated desire for sovereignty and non-interference in its internal affairs.

In recent years, China's approach to global security has been characterized by a combination of pragmatism and assertiveness. On one hand, China has been actively participating in international security institutions, such as the United Nations, and has been a major contributor to global security efforts. On the other hand, it has also been asserting its own interests and challenging the dominance of Western powers in global security affairs.

This chapter will explore the key elements of China's approach to global security, including its views on international law, its role in global security institutions, and its approach to regional security issues. We will also examine the implications of China's approach for the United States and other major global powers. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of China's approach to global security and its impact on the international community.




### Subsection: 19.2a Chinese Role in Global Trade

China's role in global trade has been a significant factor in its approach to the global economy. As the world's largest trading nation, China's economic policies and strategies have had a profound impact on the global trading system.

#### China's Integration in the Global Trading System

China's integration in the global trading system has been a key aspect of its economic policies. Despite the embargo during the Opium Wars, China continued to be a major player in global trade. The country's trade with Japan continued unobstructed, and it was able to maintain its integration in the world trading system through various means, including smuggling and trade through Southeast Asian ports.

China's desire for European goods such as silk and porcelain led to a trade deficit, which was made up for by trading silver. This trade deficit was further exacerbated by the discovery of vast amounts of silver in the Americas and Japan, which fueled the global trade economy.

#### China's Role in the Silver Trade

The silver trade played a crucial role in China's global trade. From 1500 to 1800, Mexico and Peru produced about 80% of the world's silver, with 30% of it eventually ending up in China. The silver from the Americas and Japan flowed across the Atlantic and Pacific Oceans, with major outposts for the silver trade located in Southeast Asian countries such as the Philippines.

The city of Manila served as a primary outpost for the exchange of goods between the Americas, Japan, India, Indonesia, and China. The galleon trade, supplied by merchants largely from port areas of Fujian, was a major source of revenue for the Spanish Empire and a fundamental source of income for Spanish colonists in the Philippine Islands.

#### China's Impact on Global Trade

China's role in global trade has been significant. Its economic policies and strategies have not only influenced the global trading system but have also shaped its relationships with other countries. China's economic power and influence, as well as its economic diplomacy, have been met with both admiration and criticism from other countries.

Despite its economic power and influence, China's approach to global trade has also led to economic conflicts with other countries. The United States, in particular, has been critical of China's economic policies, particularly its trade practices and intellectual property rights. These conflicts have led to trade disputes and tensions between the two countries, highlighting the complex nature of China's role in global trade.




### Subsection: 19.2b Chinese Role in Global Finance

China's role in global finance has been a crucial aspect of its approach to the global economy. As the world's largest trading nation, China's economic policies and strategies have had a profound impact on the global financial system.

#### China's Integration in the Global Financial System

China's integration in the global financial system has been a key aspect of its economic policies. Despite the country's isolationist policies in the early 20th century, China's economic growth and increasing global trade have led to its integration in the global financial system.

China's desire for foreign investment and technology has led to the establishment of special economic zones, such as Shenzhen and Zhuhai, which have been instrumental in attracting foreign capital and technology. This has not only boosted China's economic growth but has also led to its integration in the global financial system.

#### China's Role in Global Finance

China's role in global finance has been significant. As the world's largest holder of foreign reserves, China plays a crucial role in the global financial system. Its investments in foreign assets, particularly in the United States, have been a key factor in the global financial system.

China's role in global finance is not limited to its investments. The country's economic policies, such as its currency management and trade policies, have also had a significant impact on the global financial system. For instance, China's currency management, which involves pegging the renminbi to the US dollar, has been a subject of debate among economists. Some argue that this policy has led to an undervalued renminbi, giving Chinese exports an unfair advantage in the global market.

#### China's Impact on Global Finance

China's role in global finance has been significant. Its economic policies and strategies have not only influenced the global financial system but have also shaped its relations with other countries. For instance, China's investments in other countries have been a source of tension, particularly in the United States, where concerns have been raised about the potential loss of jobs and technology.

China's role in global finance has also led to its increasing influence in international financial institutions, such as the International Monetary Fund (IMF) and the World Bank. As the world's largest economy, China's voice in these institutions has become increasingly important, leading to debates about the need for reforms in these institutions to reflect China's growing economic power.

In conclusion, China's role in global finance has been a crucial aspect of its approach to the global economy. Its integration in the global financial system, its economic policies, and its increasing influence in international financial institutions have had a profound impact on the global financial system and its relations with other countries.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to the global economy. We have seen how China's economic policies and strategies have evolved over time, from a closed and centrally planned economy to a more open and market-oriented one. We have also examined the role of China in the global economy, as a major trading partner and investor for many countries around the world.

China's economic rise has been a significant factor in shaping the global economy. Its rapid economic growth has led to a shift in the balance of economic power, with China becoming the world's second-largest economy. This has had a profound impact on the global economic landscape, with many countries seeking to engage with China and benefit from its economic growth.

However, China's economic policies and strategies have also faced criticism. Some argue that China's economic policies, particularly its currency management and trade practices, have contributed to global economic imbalances and tensions. Others argue that China's economic growth has been driven by unsustainable levels of investment and debt, which could lead to future economic challenges.

Despite these challenges, China's role in the global economy is likely to continue to grow in the coming years. As China becomes an even more significant economic power, it will continue to shape the global economy in profound ways. Understanding China's approach to the global economy is therefore crucial for anyone seeking to navigate the complexities of the global economic landscape.

China's approach to global security is shaped by its unique historical and cultural background. The country's long history of Confucian philosophy, which emphasizes harmony and non-confrontation, has influenced its foreign policy, including its approach to security. This chapter will explore how these philosophical underpinnings have shaped China's approach to global security.

Furthermore, this chapter will examine the key principles that guide China's approach to global security. These principles include the concept of non-interference in the internal affairs of other countries, the promotion of peaceful coexistence, and the pursuit of a peaceful rise. ### Subsection: 19.2c Chinese Role in Global Development

China's role in global development has been a topic of great interest and debate. As the world's largest economy and a major player in international relations, China's actions and policies have a significant impact on global development.

#### China's Role in Global Development

China's role in global development is multifaceted. On one hand, China's economic growth and development have been a model for many developing countries. Its rapid industrialization and urbanization have been seen as a testament to the power of capitalism and market-oriented reforms. However, China's economic growth has also been accompanied by significant social and environmental challenges, leading to criticism of its development model.

On the other hand, China's economic power has allowed it to play a major role in global development initiatives. The country has been a key contributor to international development agencies such as the World Bank and the International Monetary Fund. It has also been a major donor to developing countries, providing significant amounts of aid and investment.

#### China's Belt and Road Initiative

One of the most significant initiatives in China's global development strategy is the Belt and Road Initiative (BRI). Launched in 2013, the BRI is a massive infrastructure and development project that aims to connect China with Europe, Africa, and other parts of the world through a network of roads, railways, ports, and other infrastructure.

The BRI has been a subject of both praise and criticism. Supporters argue that it will boost economic growth and development in participating countries, while critics raise concerns about the potential for debt-trap diplomacy and the environmental impact of the project.

#### China's Role in Global Development: A Mixed Record

China's role in global development is a mixed record. While its economic growth and development have been a model for many developing countries, its development model has also been criticized for its social and environmental challenges. Its role in global development initiatives, such as the Belt and Road Initiative, has also been a subject of both praise and criticism. As China continues to play a major role in global development, its actions and policies will continue to be a topic of great interest and debate.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the Chinese approach to the global economy. We have seen how China's economic policies have evolved over time, from a closed and centrally planned system to a more open and market-oriented one. We have also examined the key drivers of China's economic growth, including its large domestic market, low labor costs, and aggressive investment in infrastructure and technology.

One of the most significant aspects of China's approach to the global economy is its emphasis on economic nationalism. This approach, which prioritizes the interests of the Chinese economy over those of other countries, has been a major factor in China's economic success. However, it has also led to tensions with other major powers, particularly the United States, over issues such as intellectual property rights and market access.

Another key aspect of China's approach to the global economy is its Belt and Road Initiative (BRI). This massive infrastructure and development project, which aims to connect China with Europe, Africa, and other parts of the world, has been a major source of controversy. Some view it as a way for China to expand its economic and political influence, while others see it as a way to promote economic growth and development in the participating countries.

Overall, China's approach to the global economy is complex and constantly evolving. As it continues to grow and assert its economic power, it will be interesting to see how its policies and strategies evolve in the coming years.

China's approach to international organizations is shaped by its historical and cultural background. As a country with a long history of isolation and self-sufficiency, China has traditionally been skeptical of international organizations. However, with its rise as a global power, China has become more actively involved in these organizations, using them as a means to achieve its strategic objectives.

## Chapter 20: Chinese Approach to International Organizations




### Conclusion

China's approach to the global economy has been a topic of great interest and debate among scholars and policymakers. As the world's second-largest economy, China's actions have a significant impact on the global economic landscape. In this chapter, we have explored the key aspects of China's approach to the global economy, including its economic policies, trade practices, and investment strategies.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that China's economic policies have been a major driver of its economic growth. The country's emphasis on state-led development, combined with its commitment to economic liberalization and integration into the global economy, has allowed it to achieve impressive economic growth. However, this approach has also raised concerns about China's economic dominance and its impact on other countries.

China's trade policies have been a subject of controversy, with some arguing that the country's currency manipulation and trade imbalances have contributed to global economic imbalances. However, China has also been a major driver of global trade, and its Belt and Road Initiative has the potential to further boost global trade and economic growth.

Finally, China's investment strategies have been a key factor in its economic rise. The country's state-owned enterprises have played a crucial role in driving investment and economic growth, but there have also been concerns about their lack of transparency and potential for market distortion.

In conclusion, China's approach to the global economy has been shaped by a combination of economic policies, trade practices, and investment strategies. While there have been concerns and criticisms, China's economic rise has also brought significant benefits to the global economy. As the country continues to play a major role in the global economy, it will be important for policymakers and scholars to closely monitor and analyze its economic policies and practices.

# Chinese Foreign Policy: International Relations and Strategy

## Chapter 20: Chinese Approach to Global Politics




### Introduction

China's approach to the global environment has been a topic of great interest and concern in recent years. As the world's largest emitter of greenhouse gases, China's actions have a significant impact on the global climate. In this chapter, we will explore the Chinese approach to the global environment, examining their policies, strategies, and challenges in addressing environmental issues.

China's approach to the global environment is shaped by its unique economic, social, and political context. The country's rapid economic growth and industrialization have led to significant environmental degradation, including air and water pollution, deforestation, and loss of biodiversity. As a result, the Chinese government has recognized the need to address these issues and has implemented various policies and initiatives to promote sustainable development.

One of the key aspects of China's approach to the global environment is its commitment to reducing greenhouse gas emissions. In 2020, China announced its goal to achieve carbon neutrality by 2060, which means that it aims to balance the amount of carbon dioxide it emits with the amount it removes from the atmosphere. This is a significant step towards addressing climate change and reducing the country's environmental impact.

Another important aspect of China's approach is its focus on sustainable development. The Chinese government has recognized that economic growth cannot come at the expense of the environment, and has implemented policies to promote sustainable practices in various sectors, including energy, transportation, and agriculture. This includes initiatives such as the Belt and Road Initiative, which aims to promote sustainable infrastructure development in countries along the Belt and Road.

However, China's approach to the global environment also faces challenges. The country's rapid economic growth and urbanization have led to significant environmental degradation, and there are concerns about the effectiveness of some of its policies and initiatives. Additionally, China's approach to the global environment is often met with criticism and scrutiny from other countries, particularly the United States.

In this chapter, we will delve deeper into these topics, examining the Chinese approach to the global environment in detail. We will explore the country's policies, strategies, and challenges, and discuss the implications for the global community. By understanding China's approach to the global environment, we can gain valuable insights into the country's foreign policy and its role in shaping the future of our planet.




### Subsection: 20.1a Role of Global Environment in Foreign Policy

The global environment plays a crucial role in shaping China's foreign policy. As a major global power, China's actions and policies have a significant impact on the international community. The country's approach to the global environment is shaped by its economic, social, and political context, as well as its historical and cultural traditions.

China's economic growth and industrialization have led to significant environmental degradation, including air and water pollution, deforestation, and loss of biodiversity. As a result, the Chinese government has recognized the need to address these issues and has implemented various policies and initiatives to promote sustainable development. This includes the country's commitment to reducing greenhouse gas emissions and achieving carbon neutrality by 2060.

In addition to its domestic policies, China's approach to the global environment is also shaped by its foreign policy objectives. The country's Belt and Road Initiative, for example, aims to promote sustainable infrastructure development in countries along the Belt and Road. This initiative not only addresses China's own environmental concerns, but also helps to improve the environmental conditions in other countries.

Furthermore, China's approach to the global environment is also influenced by its historical and cultural traditions. The country has a long history of valuing nature and promoting harmony between humans and the environment. This traditional philosophy has been incorporated into modern Chinese environmental policies, with the concept of "ecological civilization" being a key principle in China's approach to the global environment.

However, China's approach to the global environment also faces challenges. The country's rapid economic growth and urbanization have led to significant environmental degradation, and there are concerns about the potential negative impacts of China's environmental policies on its economy and development. Additionally, China's approach to the global environment has been criticized by some countries and organizations, with concerns about the country's lack of transparency and accountability in its environmental policies.

In conclusion, the global environment plays a crucial role in shaping China's foreign policy. The country's economic, social, and political context, as well as its historical and cultural traditions, all contribute to its approach to the global environment. While there are challenges and criticisms, China's commitment to addressing environmental issues and promoting sustainable development is a key aspect of its foreign policy.





### Subsection: 20.1b Chinese Approach to Global Environment

China's approach to the global environment is shaped by its economic, social, and political context, as well as its historical and cultural traditions. The country's economic growth and industrialization have led to significant environmental degradation, including air and water pollution, deforestation, and loss of biodiversity. As a result, the Chinese government has recognized the need to address these issues and has implemented various policies and initiatives to promote sustainable development.

One of the key principles guiding China's approach to the global environment is the concept of "ecological civilization." This concept emphasizes the harmonious relationship between humans and nature, and the need for sustainable development that balances economic growth with environmental protection. The Chinese government has made promoting ecological civilization a top priority in its foreign policy, and has implemented various initiatives to achieve this goal.

One of these initiatives is the Belt and Road Initiative (BRI), which aims to promote sustainable infrastructure development in countries along the Belt and Road. This initiative not only addresses China's own environmental concerns, but also helps to improve the environmental conditions in other countries. The BRI includes provisions for sustainable development and environmental protection, and has been praised for its potential to address global environmental issues.

In addition to its domestic policies and initiatives, China has also been actively involved in international efforts to address global environmental issues. The country has signed and ratified various international environmental agreements, including the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change and the Paris Agreement. China has also been a major contributor to the Green Climate Fund, which aims to help developing countries adapt to and mitigate the impacts of climate change.

However, China's approach to the global environment also faces challenges. The country's rapid economic growth and urbanization have led to significant environmental degradation, and there are concerns about the potential negative impacts of China's environmental policies on its own citizens and the global community. For example, some critics argue that China's reliance on coal and other fossil fuels for its economic growth has contributed to global climate change and air pollution.

Despite these challenges, China's approach to the global environment has been praised for its commitment to sustainable development and its efforts to address global environmental issues. As the country continues to grow and play a larger role in the international community, its approach to the global environment will continue to shape its foreign policy and have a significant impact on the global environment.





### Subsection: 20.1c Impact on International Relations

China's approach to the global environment has had a significant impact on its international relations. As one of the world's largest economies and emitters of greenhouse gases, China's actions and policies regarding the environment are closely watched by other countries. This has led to both criticism and praise for China's approach to the global environment.

On one hand, China's economic growth and industrialization have been criticized for their negative impact on the environment. The country's heavy reliance on coal and other fossil fuels has contributed to global climate change, and its rapid urbanization and industrialization have led to significant air and water pollution. This has strained China's relationships with other countries, particularly those with strong environmental policies and concerns.

However, China's efforts to address these issues have also been praised and have improved its relationships with other countries. The Belt and Road Initiative, for example, has been welcomed by many developing countries as a way to improve their infrastructure and promote sustainable development. This has helped to strengthen China's relationships with these countries and has also improved its image as a responsible global player.

In addition, China's commitment to international environmental agreements has also improved its relationships with other countries. By signing and ratifying these agreements, China has shown its willingness to work towards global solutions to environmental issues. This has helped to improve its relationships with other major powers, such as the United States and the European Union, and has also strengthened its relationships with developing countries.

Overall, China's approach to the global environment has had a significant impact on its international relations. While its past actions have been criticized, its recent efforts to address environmental issues have helped to improve its relationships with other countries and have strengthened its position as a global leader. As China continues to address its environmental challenges, its approach to the global environment will continue to shape its international relations.





### Subsection: 20.2a Chinese Role in Climate Change Negotiations

China's role in climate change negotiations has been a topic of great interest and debate in recent years. As the world's largest emitter of greenhouse gases, China's actions and policies have a significant impact on global climate change. In this section, we will examine China's role in climate change negotiations, including its historical stance and recent developments.

#### Historical Stance

Historically, China's stance on climate change has been shaped by its economic development and its relationship with other major powers. As a developing country, China has argued that it should not be held to the same standards as developed countries in terms of emissions reductions. This is based on the principle of "common but differentiated responsibilities," which holds that since China is still developing, its abilities and capacities to reduce emissions are comparatively lower than developed countries'.

However, as China's economic power and global influence have grown, its stance on climate change has evolved. In 2015, China announced its support for the "common but differentiated responsibilities" principle, marking a significant shift in its approach to climate change. This shift has been driven by a combination of domestic concerns, such as air and water pollution, and international pressure, particularly from the United States.

#### Recent Developments

In recent years, China has taken a more proactive role in climate change negotiations. In 2012, it established the National Center for Climate Change Strategy and International Cooperation, which works closely with international research institutions and think tanks. This center is part of China's effort to develop world-class research in the area of climate change.

In 2018, China urged countries to continue to support the Paris agreement, even in the wake of the United States' withdrawal in 2017. This demonstrates China's commitment to international efforts to address climate change.

#### Carbon Neutrality by 2060

In 2020, Chinese leader Xi Jinping announced at the UN General Assembly in New York that his country will end its contribution to global heating and achieve carbon neutrality by 2060. This is a significant commitment, as it represents a major shift in China's approach to climate change. By adopting "more vigorous policies and measures," China aims to reduce its carbon emissions and contribute to global efforts to limit global warming.

#### Conclusion

China's role in climate change negotiations has evolved significantly in recent years. While it has historically argued for a differentiated approach to emissions reductions, it has now taken a more proactive role in international efforts to address climate change. Its commitment to carbon neutrality by 2060 demonstrates its growing commitment to addressing global environmental issues. However, there is still ongoing debate over China's eco-cities and its impact on international relations. 





### Subsection: 20.2b Chinese Role in Biodiversity Conservation

China's role in biodiversity conservation has been a topic of increasing concern in recent years. As one of the world's most biodiverse countries, China is home to a vast array of plant and animal species, many of which are found nowhere else on Earth. However, this biodiversity is under threat from a variety of factors, including habitat destruction, pollution, and overexploitation of natural resources.

#### Historical Stance

Historically, China's stance on biodiversity conservation has been shaped by its economic development and its relationship with other major powers. As a developing country, China has argued that it should not be held to the same standards as developed countries in terms of biodiversity conservation. This is based on the principle of "common but differentiated responsibilities," which holds that since China is still developing, its abilities and capacities to protect biodiversity are comparatively lower than developed countries'.

However, as China's economic power and global influence have grown, its stance on biodiversity conservation has evolved. In 2015, China announced its support for the "common but differentiated responsibilities" principle, marking a significant shift in its approach to biodiversity conservation. This shift has been driven by a combination of domestic concerns, such as air and water pollution, and international pressure, particularly from the United States.

#### Recent Developments

In recent years, China has taken a more proactive role in biodiversity conservation. In 2018, China announced a new national strategy for biodiversity conservation, which includes a goal of protecting 30% of its land and water areas by 2030. This strategy also includes measures to address the main threats to biodiversity, such as habitat destruction and overexploitation of natural resources.

China has also been working to improve its legal framework for biodiversity conservation. In 2019, the country passed a new law on the protection of biological diversity, which aims to strengthen the management and conservation of biodiversity. This law includes provisions for the establishment of protected areas, the regulation of trade in endangered species, and the promotion of sustainable use of biodiversity.

#### Chinese Role in Biodiversity Conservation

China's role in biodiversity conservation has been a topic of increasing concern in recent years. As one of the world's most biodiverse countries, China is home to a vast array of plant and animal species, many of which are found nowhere else on Earth. #### Chinese Role in Biodiversity Conservation

China's role in biodiversity conservation has been a topic of increasing concern in recent years. As one of the world's most biodiverse countries, China is home to a vast array of plant and animal species, many of which are found nowhere else on Earth. However, this biodiversity is under threat from a variety of factors, including habitat destruction, pollution, and overexploitation of natural resources.

China's role in biodiversity conservation is multifaceted. On one hand, China has been a major contributor to the loss of biodiversity, due to its rapid economic development and increasing consumption of natural resources. On the other hand, China has also been a leader in the development and implementation of biodiversity conservation strategies.

One of the key areas where China has made significant progress is in the establishment of protected areas. As of 2019, China has established over 2,349 nature reserves, covering a total area of 149.95 million hectares, or 15% of its total land area. These reserves are home to a diverse array of plant and animal species, and play a crucial role in protecting China's biodiversity.

In addition to protected areas, China has also been working to improve its legal framework for biodiversity conservation. The new law on the protection of biological diversity, passed in 2019, aims to strengthen the management and conservation of biodiversity. This law includes provisions for the establishment of protected areas, the regulation of trade in endangered species, and the promotion of sustainable use of biodiversity.

China's role in biodiversity conservation is also evident in its efforts to address the main threats to biodiversity. In 2018, China announced a new national strategy for biodiversity conservation, which includes a goal of protecting 30% of its land and water areas by 2030. This strategy also includes measures to address the main threats to biodiversity, such as habitat destruction and overexploitation of natural resources.

Overall, China's role in biodiversity conservation is complex and multifaceted. While it has been a major contributor to the loss of biodiversity, it has also been a leader in the development and implementation of biodiversity conservation strategies. As China continues to grow and develop, it will be crucial for the country to prioritize biodiversity conservation in order to protect its unique and diverse ecosystems for future generations.





### Subsection: 20.2c Chinese Role in Sustainable Development

China's role in sustainable development has been a topic of increasing interest in recent years. As the world's largest emitter of greenhouse gases, China's actions have a significant impact on the global climate. However, China has also been a leader in renewable energy and has made significant strides in reducing its carbon intensity.

#### Historical Stance

Historically, China's stance on sustainable development has been shaped by its economic development and its relationship with other major powers. As a developing country, China has argued that it should not be held to the same standards as developed countries in terms of environmental protection. This is based on the principle of "common but differentiated responsibilities," which holds that since China is still developing, its abilities and capacities to protect the environment are comparatively lower than developed countries'.

However, as China's economic power and global influence have grown, its stance on sustainable development has evolved. In 2015, China announced its support for the "common but differentiated responsibilities" principle, marking a significant shift in its approach to sustainable development. This shift has been driven by a combination of domestic concerns, such as air and water pollution, and international pressure, particularly from the United States.

#### Recent Developments

In recent years, China has taken a more proactive role in sustainable development. In 2017, China announced its "Made in China 2025" plan, which aims to transform the country into a global leader in advanced manufacturing and technology. This plan includes a focus on sustainable development, with a goal of reducing carbon emissions and promoting the use of renewable energy.

China has also been a major investor in renewable energy projects around the world. In 2019, China invested $103 billion in renewable energy, more than any other country. This investment has helped to reduce China's carbon intensity and has also created jobs and economic opportunities in other countries.

#### The Belt and Road Initiative

One of the most significant developments in China's approach to sustainable development is its Belt and Road Initiative (BRI). Launched in 2013, the BRI is a massive infrastructure and development project that aims to connect China with Europe, Africa, and other parts of the world through a network of roads, railways, ports, and other infrastructure.

The BRI has been criticized for its potential environmental impacts, particularly in terms of deforestation and pollution. However, China has also made efforts to incorporate sustainable development principles into the BRI. For example, the BRI includes a focus on green infrastructure, such as renewable energy projects and sustainable transportation systems. China has also established a Green Belt and Road Fund to finance sustainable development projects along the BRI.

#### Conclusion

China's role in sustainable development has evolved significantly in recent years. While it has faced criticism for its environmental policies, China has also made significant strides in reducing its carbon intensity and promoting sustainable development. The Belt and Road Initiative presents both challenges and opportunities for sustainable development, and China's approach to the BRI will be a crucial factor in determining its impact on the global environment.
